AliceAdventuresinWonderlandbyLewisCarroll.txt\tbank, and of having nothing to do: once or twice she had peeped into the

AliceAdventuresinWonderlandbyLewisCarroll.txt\tCHAPTER II. The Pool of Tears
AliceAdventuresinWonderlandbyLewisCarroll.txt\t

AliceAdventuresinWonderlandbyLewisCarroll.txt\t

AliceAdventuresinWonderlandbyLewisCarroll.txt\t

AliceAdventuresinWonderlandbyLewisCarroll.txt\t

AliceAdventuresinWonderlandbyLewisCarroll.txt\ttried to beat them off, and found herself lying on the bank, with her

AliceAdventuresinWonderlandbyLewisCarroll.txt\t‘Oh, I’ve had such a curious dream!’ said Alice, and she told her

AliceAdventuresinWonderlandbyLewisCarroll.txt\tAlice got up and ran off, thinking while she ran, as well she might,

AliceAdventuresinWonderlandbyLewisCarroll.txt\twonderful Adventures, till she too began dreaming after a fashion, and

AliceAdventuresinWonderlandbyLewisCarroll.txt\tlisten, the whole place around her became alive with the strange creatures
